Jamison Brereton

61 (887)
All Gods
N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha M─Бnava
27 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
The near impenetrability of this hymn with all its poetic tricks and semantic eva sions produces a certain despair in the translator, and it is no wonder that even sensible and thoughtful interpreters have clearly gone astrayтАФas, no doubt, have the present ones. Much of what follows is tentative and provisional, but we have attempted to give an interpretation that is internally consistent and depends as little as possible on outside and post-R╠еgvedic materials.
This hymn and the next one are attributed by the Anukramaс╣З─л to N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha M─Бnava. Although the Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa contains a story about N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha (AiB V.14), it is generally agreed that this later tale has little to do with this hymn and cannot explain its mysteries. We would go further and suggest that the sup
posed poetтАЩs name has simply been extracted from verse 18, where it is, in our view, the name or epithet of a different participant. We are inclined to ascribe the hymn rather to Kakс╣г─лvant, the crafty poet of I.116тАУ126, or a descendant or would-be epigone of his: Kakс╣г─лvant is mentioned in verse 16, and the hymn has certain con
nections with Kakс╣г─лvantтАЩs oeuvre, especially I.121.
The hymn consists of several different sections, but we believe that these are all linked through the dawn sacrifice and the participants therein, particularly Dawn herself, Agni, the A┼Ыvins, and Indra. Two mythological sections treat different myths about Dawn, and these are sandwiched between sections apparently depict
ing and meditating upon an early-morning sacrifice and the dakс╣гiс╣З─Бs, or priestly gifts, distributed there.
The first four verses concern a man called T┼лrvay─Бс╣Зa, who in a verbal contest produces a supremely effective verbal formulation, which brings the A┼Ыvins to the sacrifice and which also prompts liberal gifts to himself and which rescues or oth erwise provides help to his parents and priests. His effective speech is contrasted with that of Cyav─Бna (a client of the A┼Ыvins in other circumstances), who produces1474 X.61
only тАЬsweet dregsтАЭ (vs. 2), while T┼лrvay─Бс╣ЗaтАЩs speech is likened to gushing semen. His invocation to the A┼Ыvins is given verbatim in verse 4.
The next four verses treat the shocking story of HeavenтАЩs incest with his daughter, Dawn. This is a favorite myth of the middle Vedic period (see Jamison 1991: 294тАУ 96), but nowhere is it as graphically, if fragmentarily, treated as it is here. She finally escapes (vs. 8), but before this happens, some of his semen is spilled on the ground (vs. 7), indeed on the ritual ground (vs. 6). From this semen the ritual fire is fash ioned (vss. 7 and 9). Thus, though the rape of HeavenтАЩs daughter is depicted as brutal, it results in the creation of the central ritual substanceтАФas so often, around the world, in myths of cosmic rape and incest the taboo sexual encounter is primally creative. It seems likely that the comparison of T┼лrvay─Бс╣ЗaтАЩs verbal production with semen, in conjunction with the overall theme of dawn sacrifice, prompted the telling of this story in just this place.
Verse 9 and the birth of fire form the transition to the next mythological sec tion, the freeing of Dawn from the Vala cave by the Aс╣Еgirases and Navagvas (vss. 9тАУ13). Verses 9тАУ11 all begin тАЬright awayтАЭ (makс╣г┼л╠Б). As noted, verse 9 treats the newly created fire. In verse 10 (at least in our reading of it) the Navagvas attempt to free Dawn from her тАЬprotector,тАЭ the Vala cave. In verse 11 the mythic motifs of the Dawn cow and her milk and of Agni, the product of HeavenтАЩs semen, are brought togetherтАФthe motifs that are sacrificially found together in the dawn sacrifice. The Aс╣Еgiras story is continued in the two following verses (12тАУ13), though the dramatic high point has already been reached.
The subject changes abruptly with the next verses (14тАУ15), back to the ritual fire and the sacrifice to which the A┼Ыvins will come. There then follows a section that has led many commentators (see especially Oldenberg and Geldner) to con struct elaborate family trees and тАЬback-storiesтАЭ for the poet, who is supposed to be seeking either a new, adoptive father (Geldner) or a new varс╣Зa (Oldenberg). In our view these ingenious constructions are unnecessary and misguided. Instead the poet, perhaps Kakс╣г─лvant (16c), is presenting his patron with what appears at first to be a pra┼Ыasti, an encomium, but which then gently mocks him for his pretentions and for perceived stinginess. Verse 16 is a fine straightforward piece of praise, attributing grand titles and qualities to the king, in our view the poetтАЩs patron. Verse 17 is more equivocal. The king, the sacrificer, is тАЬof two lin
eagesтАЭ: this is the term that provoked the family-tree constructions of Oldenberg and Geldner. We think rather that the poet is suggesting that the king is kin to both the human and divine racesтАФor that the king so believes (see the next verse). But the poet also says that the king ought to milk the cow that yields sap but does not give birthтАФwhich may be an allusion to the kingтАЩs slowness to produce dakс╣гiс╣З─Бs for his poet, who points out in the second half of the verse that he him
self is doing his job in producing poetry. Verse 18 seems to us to embody the pretensions of the patron-king. His name or epithet is N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha, тАЬnearest to the navelтАЭ: тАЬnavelтАЭ is a standard metaphor for origin and close kinship (especially the point of origin of two disparate groups), as well as for the focal point of the sacrifice or indeed the world itself. (This epithet must be very old, as the same word is found in Younger Avestan nab─Бnazdi┼бta тАЬclosely related, next of kin.тАЭ) And in the second half of the verse he wonders aloud how high his тАЬnavelтАЭ is, relative to an unidentified other, then boasts of the unbroken chain of generations that links him to the original navel. He gets his comeuppance in the next verse (19), where the god Agni lays claim to the real navel, the gods, the two births, and the cow and her products.
With the patron put in his place, the hymn now turns to a depiction of the dawn sacrifice, or rather its conclusion, in five verses (20тАУ24), each beginning with the word ├бdha тАЬ(and) now.тАЭ The dakс╣гiс╣З─Бs are now properly given (see 21ab), and the poet therefore calls on the gods for honor and protection for the patrons (vss. 22тАУ23). In the final verse of this sequence (24) the poet and his colleagues appear to be poised to express their final prayers (24b), prayers found in the final verse (27). In between are two verses (25тАУ26) that ascribe тАЬgood lineageтАЭ to an unidenti
fied subject, who both takes pleasure in a praise hymn and performs ritual service. The тАЬgood lineageтАЭ reminds us of the patronтАЩs claims to distinguished kinship earlier in the hymn, which were trumped by the god Agni. In these two verses we believe that the poet deliberately left the subject unidentified and that he meant the verses to be read with both Agni and himself (the poet) as potential subjects, thus associating himself with the fine family and divine relations that the patron craved.
Needless to say, this is a very speculative reading of the poem, and many details remain unaccounted for. It is to be hoped that further progress can be made in its interpretation, within a R╠еgvedic context.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe fierce-voiced (N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha repeated) through his intelligence this praise of Rudra, in themidst of the ceremony at the assembly (of the Aс╣Еgirasas), which (praise) his parents, making (the partition) andhis brothers engaged in giving (the shares accomplished); he perfected the seven priests (therewith) on the dayon which the rite was to be matured.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A legend from Aitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 5.14: The brothers ofN─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha partioned among themselves to his exclusion the whole of the paternal wealth, while he wasengaged in his religious studies. Upon completing the studies, N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha applied to his father for hisportion, but there was nothing left, and his brothers refused to give any of their shares. As a compensation, Manurecommended to him to apply to the Aс╣Еgirasas, who were engaged in a sacrifice for obtaining Svarga, buthaving come to the sixth day, were so perplexed by the number of the mantras, that they could go no furtherwithout assistance, N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha went to them, and repeated for them this and the following s┼лkta.Through the efficacy of these two s┼лktas, they went to heaven, leaving to him the remainder of the sacrifice, athousand head of cattle. As N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha was waking off with them, he was stopped by Rudra, seated on ablack corpse, who claimed whatever was left at a sacrifice as his right. Referring to Manu, the patriarch admittedthe law, and N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha relinquished the cattle to Rudra who, in reward of his ready acknowledgement ofthe truth, presented the cows to him

Jamison Brereton

Here is a Rudrian formulation right to the point, (which) he whose speech is welcome (produced) with his mental force at a contest
in skill,
(a formulation) that, standing ready for liberality, will effectively guide across his two parents and, on the fifth [?] day, the seven Hotars.

Griffith

THE welcome speaker in the storm of battle uttered with might this prayer to win the Asvins,
When the most liberal God, for Paktha, rescued his parents, and assailed the seven Hotras.

Grassmann

Dies an den Rudra gerichtete Gebet [vollbrachte] der angenehm redende mit Weisheit im Eifer w├дhrend des Wettkampfes, als er gesch├дftig und freigiebig seine Aeltern beschenkte und beim Paktha die sieben Priester [im Wettkampf] ├╝berwand [? ├бhan als Loc. von ├бhan gefasst gibt einen noch weniger zusagenden Sinn].

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(I call you to these) oblations, to which hastening, (A┼Ыvins), swift as thought at the invitation of theworshipper, you rejoice my (worshipper) who, affluent in the wealth of sacrifice, mixes (the oblation) with hisfingers in your presence, (holding) in his hand the sacrifice intended (for you).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 7.170: the verse is said tobe addressed to the two priests, the adhvaryu and pratiprasth─Бt─Б, engaged in mixing curds with ground barleyin the Manthigraha

Jamison Brereton

(T┼лrvay─Бс╣Зa)тАФto whose invocations you two [=A┼Ыvins] run and win inspired words, (produced) by his skill, that are like sharp thinking,
he who, powerfully manly, with arrows in his hand, brought his aim to fulfillment.

Griffith

To his oblations, swift as thought, ye hurried, and welcomed eagerly the prayers he offered.
With arrows in his hand the Very Mighty forced from him all obedience of a servant.

Geldner

Bei dessen Anrufungen ihr beide scharf wie der Gedanke mit aller Kraft herbeieilend die Reden gut aufnehmet, der mit den Pfeilen in seiner Hand das Ziel traf, der Mannhafte.

Grassmann

Bei welchen Opferspenden ihr beiden kr├дftig laufenden [A├зvinen] dem gleichsam gesch├дrften Geist des S├дngers hold seid, welcher sehr mannhaft mit den Fingern am Arme dessen [etwa des Agni?] Absicht erf├╝llte.

English translation:

тАЬWhen the dark night rettires before the purple oxen (of the chariot of the dawn), I invoke you,A┼Ыvinschildren of heaven; be desirous of my sacrifice; come to my food and to my viands like (two horses) eatingtogether, oblivious of offence.тАЭ

Children of heaven: divo nap─Бta = not making heaven to fall

Jamison Brereton

тАЬWhen black (Night) is sitting among the ruddy cows (of Dawn), o A┼Ыvins, I call upon you two, the sons of heaven.
Pursue my sacrifice, come here to my food, like winners to refreshment, as the two of whom no deception can be remembered.тАЭ

I call on you the Sons of Dyaus, the Asvins, that a dark cow to my red kine be added.
Enjoy my sacrifice, come to my viands contented, not deceiving expectation. '

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Rudra), the benefactor of man, whose eager, virile energy was developed, drew it back whendisseminated (for the genitive ration of offfspring); again the irresistible (Rudra) concentrates (the energy) which wascommunicated to his maiden daughter.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This and the following two с╣Ыcas seem to refer to the begetting of Rudraby Praj─Бpati; there is a mix-up with the legend of Brahma’s incestuous passion for his daughter. According to theAitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 3.33, she was the heaven or the dawn

Again he tears out from the maiden, his daughter, what had been тАЬbrought to bearтАЭ on herтАФhe the unassailable.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhen the father united with the daughter, then associating with the earth, he sprinkled it with theeffusion; then the thoughtful gods begot Brahma; they fabricated the lord of the hearth (of sacrifice); the defenderof sacred rites.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Lord of the hearth of sacrifice: or v─Бstoс╣гpati. He is always considered to be Rudra, as in theAitareya Br─Бhmaс╣Зa 3.33. The gods, incensed by Brahma’s wickedness, seek for someone to put him to death;but, each feeling his own inability, they create Rudra for the purpose. Rudra wounds Praj─Бpati, who hadassumed the form of a deer, and flying to heaven becomes the asterism mс╣Ыga┼Ы─лrс╣гa, the doe into which thedaughter had been changed becomes the asterism rohiс╣З─л. Rudra follows and becomes mс╣Ыgavy─Бdha

Jamison Brereton

When the father тАЬsprang onтАЭ his own daughter, he, uniting (with her), poured down his semen upon the earth.
The gods, very concerned, begat the sacred formulation, and they fashioned out (of it?) the Lord of the Dwelling Place, protector of commandments.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe, like the showerer (Indra), cast foam around in the combat, and came away from us with a niggardmind; he advances not a step, relinquishing the donations; though skilled in rapine, he seizes not these my(cows).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The verse is said to be repeated by N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha when he sees V─Бstoс╣гpati (or Rudra) coming tostop him; cast foam around: an allusion to the destruction of Namuci by Indra in the shape of the foam of the sea;relinquishing the donations: i.e., the cows given to Rudra by the Aс╣Еgirasas as dakс╣гiс╣З─Б or honorarium

Jamison Brereton

Like a bull in a contest he threw off foam. Heedless, she went away, hither and yon.
Twisting away, she hastened like the Gift-Cow on foot. [The father:] тАЬNow those caresses of mine have not grasped (her).тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe fire, harming the people, does not approach quickly (by day); the naked (r─Бkс╣гasas approach)not Agni by night; the giver of fuel, and the giver of food, he, the upholder (of the rite), is born, overcomingenemies by his might.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The fire: i.e., the fire-resembling r─Бkс╣гasas and the like

Jamison Brereton

Right away, like a chariot-horse (came) the trampling of the offspring [=Agni], and he took his seat at the udder, as one naked in the cold takes a seat close to the fire.
He gained the kindling wood and he gained the prize; he was born as the upholder, ever doing battle with his strength.

Griffith

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Aс╣Еgirasas, who were engaged in the nine months;’ ceremonial, reciting the praise suited to therite, quickly attained the friendship of the maiden; those who seated in the two seats (heaven and earth) came totheir protector, as they had no donation, milked forth the inexhaustible (waters).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The maiden: Pс╣Ыs;’ni;kaman─лyayaс╕е stuteс╕е = kanyaс╕е; the Aс╣Еgirasas attained the completion of their ceremony (by means) of thedesirable praise (taught them by N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha)? Had no donation: dakс╣гiс╣З─Бsaс╕е; the Aс╣Еgirasas beingboth yajam─Бnas and priests, there could be no dakс╣гiс╣З─Б

Jamison Brereton

Right away the Navagvas came to the fellowship of the maiden [=Dawn] and, speaking the truth, to the yoking of truth.
Those who approached the protector [=Vala?] of doubly exalted (Dawn?), though they lacked the Gift-Cow, strove to milk the
immovable ones [=Vala rocks?].

Griffith

Uttering praise to suit the rite Navagvas came speedily to win the damsel’s friendship.
They who approached the twice-strong stable’s keeper, meedless would milk the rocks that naught had shaken.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬQuickly (obtaining) the friendship of the maiden, they poured forth water like new wealth, when theyoffered to you (Indra) the pure riches, the milk of the cow, that yields ambrosia.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Pure riches: rekс╣Зas = wealth leftby a dead person n, wealth consisting of water

Jamison Brereton

Right away they hastened anew to the fellowship of the maiden and to the semen, which was like a bounty, which is just truthтАФ
your blazing legacy, which they gained through sacrifice, and the milk of the ruddy female who gives sap as milk.

Griffith

Swift was new friendship with the maid they quickly accepted it as genuine seed and bounty.
Milk which the cow Sabardugha had yielded was the bright heritage which to thee they offered.

Geldner

Alsbald nachdem sie aufs neue die Freundschaft der Jungfrau erlangt hatten, beschleunigten sie den rechten Samen wie eine Ehrengabe, den reinen Trank, den sie dir als dein Eigentum zum Opfer brachten, die Milch der immermelken Kuh.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ“When (the worshippers) find (the stalls deserted) by the cattle” (then the performer of the rite)exclaims, “(Indra), plural asing to his adorer, the affluent lord of affluence, the compassionate, the sinless, quicklyrecovers all the wealth (that has been carried off)."тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Exclaims: The words, iti brav─лti seem to apply to the wholeс╣Ыca: k─Бravaс╕е is the subject of brav─лti; or, an epithet applying to Indra

Jamison Brereton

When afterward they became aware of their separation from the livestock, he [=Br╠еhaspati or Indra] speaks thus, while bestowing (gifts) at the speaking:
тАЬThrough the goodness of the good one, the bards are blameless. He exerts control over all movable property, all the way up to cattle.тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhether Bharga is the name of that radiance, on the triple seat of which those who are gods areseated, as if in heaven, or whether it be Agni, or J─Бtavedas; invoker (of the gods), who are the ministrant priestof the sacrifice, hear our guileless invocation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

тАЬLusterтАЭ is the name (of him), to whom the gods belong, who have set him down in his triple seat like the sun, and тАЬAgni J─БtavedasтАЭ is his name. Hear us, o Hotar, as our Hotar of truth, free of deception.

Griffith

Thou, called Effulgence, in whose threefold dwelling, as in the light of heaven, the Gods are sitting,
Thou who art called Agni or Jatavedas, Priest, hear us, guileless Priest of holy worship.

Geldner

Sein Name ist Glanz, dem auch die G├╢tter geh├╢ren, die ihn auf dem dreifachen Sitze wie die Sonne eingesetzt haben. Sein Name ist Agni und Jatavedas. H├╢re auf uns, o Hotri, als der untr├╝gliche Hotri der rechten Opferordnung!

Grassmann

Der du Glanz heisst, in dessen dreifachem Sitze wie im Himmelsglanze die G├╢tter sich niederliessen, der du Agni heisst und Wesenkenner, h├╢re uns, o Priester, des heiligen Werkes wohlwollender Priester.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAnd, Indra, let those two brilliant sons of Rudra, the N─Бsaty─Бs, (be present) at my praise andsacrifice; being propitious to (me seated) on the strewn grass, as (at the sacrifice of) Manu, cheerful, liberal ofwealth to the people, deserving of adoration.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The people: i.e., to our priests

Jamison Brereton

And these two sons of Rudra, the N─Бsatyas who possess the chant, are to be greeted and offered sacrifice by me, o IndraтАФ
the two who give (gifts) to him who, like Manus, provides the twisted ritual grass; the delightful pair for whom pleasing offerings are set
out; and the two that seek sacrifice among the clans.

Griffith

And, Indra, bring, that I may laud and serve them, those Two resplendent glorious Nasatyas,
Blithe, bounteous, man-like, to the sacrificer, honoured among our men with offered viands.

Geldner

Und auch diese strahlenden, rudrischen Nasatya┬┤s will ich, um mir Beifall zu erwerben, verehren, o Indra, die dem gern spenden, der gleich Manu das Barhis umgelegt hat, die Erfreulichen, denen ein Opfermahl bereitet ist, die in den Niederlassungen Opfer erwarten.

Grassmann

Auch jene beiden pr├дchtigen, gl├дnzenden N─Б satja’s, o Indra, sollen auf mein Lob und Opfer achten, welche nach Menschenart dem Streubereiter Gaben spenden, erfreuend, sie, denen Opferspeisen vorgesetzt, und die in den H├дusern zu verehren sind.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis royal (Soma), this glorified creator, is praised (by all), and, like a sage, constituting his owncause-way, he traverses the firmament; he made Kakс╣г─лvat tremble, he (made) Agni (shake) as horses (agitate)the light- whirling, revolving-wheel (of a chariot).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This king praised here has been extolled as a ritual adept, and as inspired poet he crosses the waters, creating his own bridge.
He sets Kakс╣г─лvant atremble and also Agni, as the swift-running wheel of a steed does its wheel-rim.

Griffith

This King is praised and honoured as Ordainer: himself the bridge, the Sage speeds o’er the waters.
He hath stirred up Kaksivan, stirred up Agni, as the steed’s swift wheel drives the felly onward.

Geldner

Dieser gepriesene K├╢nig ward als Meister gelobt, und als Redner ├╝berschreitet er die Gew├дsser, sich selbst als Br├╝cke brauchend. Er machte den Kaksivat, er den Agni erzittern wie das raschlaufende Rad des Rennpferdes die Radfelge.

Grassmann

Dieser gepriesene huldvolle K├╢nig [Soma S─Бy.] wird ger├╝hmt; der weise setzt ├╝ber die Wasser, seine eignen Br├╝cken habend; er setzte den Kaksch─лvat in Bewegung und er den Agni, wie den Radkranz, wie das schnell laufende vom Renner gezogene Rad.

English translation:

тАЬThe kinsman of the two (worlds, Agni), the conveyer (of all), the sacrificer, (made) theambrosia-yielding cow, which had not given birth, to yield milk (for ┼Ъayu), when he praises Mitra, Varuс╣Зa andAryaman, with most excellent and choice hymns.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

He of two lineages, the son of Vitaraс╣Зa, the sacrificer, is to milk the milk-cow, which is sap-yielding but not giving birth,
when I enmesh Mitra and Varuс╣Зa with hymns and Aryaman with
preeminent defenses.

Griffith

Vaitarana, doubly kinsman, sacrificer, shall milk the cow who ne’er hath calved, Sabardhu,
When I encompass Varuna and Mitra with lauds, and Aryaman in safest shelter.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe kinsman of the earth, the utterer of praise (belonging) to you (who abides) in heaven,N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha, the supporter of the rite, desiring (the recompense), repeats (this praise); the (heaven) ourmost excellent bound (is the site) of the (sun), and I was after many (degrees) descended from hiс╣ГтАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha’s affinity to the sun is apparent; his father manu is the son of Vivasvat or ─Аditya; after manydegrees: katitha┼Ыcid ─Бsa = I was the completion (p┼лraс╣Зa) of many

Jamison Brereton

The patron whose lineage this is, setting your insight in heaven,
N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha [/nearest to the navel], murmurs as he quests:
тАЬIs this navel of ours highest or is his? I was the so-many-eth after
that one.тАЭ

Griffith

Their kin, the Prince in heaven, thy nearest kinsman, turning his thought to thee thus speaks in kindness:
This is our highest bond: I am his offspring. How many others came ere I succeeded?

Geldner

Dessen Verwandter, der Opferherr, auf dich im Himmel sein Denken richtend, der Nabhanedistha, fl├╝stert im Geiste weiterschauend also: Dies ist unser h├╢chster Ursprung oder auch der seine. Ich bin erst sp├дter als so und sovielter geworden.

Grassmann

Mit diesem verwandt preist dich im Himmel andachtsvoll und verlangend der glanzreiche N─Бbh─Бnedischtha; dies ist unsere h├╢chste Verwandtschaft und von ihm bin ich der Reihe nach der so und so vielste.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThis (aerial voice) is my bond of affinity; here, (in the solar orb) is my abiding-plural ce; these are myresplendent (rays); I am this all; I am the twice-born; the first-born of truth; the cow, as soon as born, milked forthidentical with ─Аditya; s─Б y─Б v─Бg asau sa ─Бdityaс╕е, that which is v─Бk is that ─Аdityaс╕е: ┼ЪatapathaBr─Бhmaс╣Зa 10.5.1.4]. the forests, terminates (in the fire of sacrifice), who upward rising, like a line, adorable, quickly subdues (hisfoes). him, unchangeable, the augmenter of happiness, his mother has brought forth.тАЭ

Si┼Ыuс╕е = ┼Ыaс╣Гsan─лyaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

[Agni:] тАЬThis, here, is my navel, and here is my seat. These gods here are mine, and here am IтАФthe wholeтАФ
having two births, first born of truth. This (earth?) here did the cow
give as her milk as she was being born.тАЭ

Griffith

Here is my kinship, here the place I dwell in: these are my Gods; I in full strength am present.
Twice-born am I, the first-born Son of Order: the Cow milked this when first she had her being.

Geldner

Dies ist mein Ursprung, hier ist mein Platz, diese G├╢tter sind mein, ich bin das vollst├дndig, der Zweimalgeborene, Erstgeborene des Gesetzes. Die Kuh hat bei ihrer Geburt dieses All als Milch von sich gegeben.

Grassmann

Dies ist meine Verwandschaft; hier ist mein Heimatsitz; hier sind meine G├╢tter, hier ich selbst in vollem Wohlsein, zweimal geboren als der erstgeborne des Rechtes, diesen Vortheil schaffte mir die geborene Milchkuh.

Jamison Brereton

Now among these (clans) the gladdening, far-radiant spoked wheel [=Agni] unhitches, the one having a double track, victorious within
the wood.
When the child of the house is like an upright line, right away the
mother gives birth to the sturdy one, who grows strong with
kindness.

Griffith

So mid these tribes he rests, the friendly envoy, borne on two paths, refulgent Lord of fuel.
When, like a line, the Babe springs up erectly, his Mother straight hath borne him strong to bless us.

Geldner

Nun kehret bei diesen Clanen der beliebte Rosselenker, der Ergl├дnzende, im Holz Siegreiche ein, der zwei Wege f├дhrt. Wann das Hauskind wie eine aufrechte Linie ist, so gebiert alsbald die Mutter den starken Liebling.

Grassmann

Dann ruht bei diesen Weibern der erfreuende strahlenreiche, rastlos th├дtige [Agni], der auf zwei Bahnen wandert und im Holze waltet; wenn der Spross [Agni] wie eine senkrechte[475] Linie sich emporrichtet, dann sogleich gebiert ihn die Mutter als den starken Heil mehrenden.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe words of the desirable (praise), of a certain tranquil person n (N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha), attain theprototype (Indra). Do you, who are the giver of wealth (Agni), hear us; offer sacrifice, you are magnified by thesincere eulogies of A┼Ыvaghna.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

A┼Ыvaghna: patronymic from ─А┼Ыvaghna, the slayer of sacrificer of a horse; aname of Manu, the father of N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha

Jamison Brereton

And now the cows of the maiden [=Dawn] have gone forth, following the distribution (of goods) of someone swollen (with wealth).
Listen to us, o you possessing good movable property; you, perform sacrifice! I have grown strong through the liberal gifts of ─А┼Ыvaghna
[/son of the horse-killer].

Griffith

Then went the milch-kine forth to please the damsel, and for the good of every man that liveth.

English translation:

тАЬDo you, Indra, king of men, who are the bearer of the thunderbolt, regard us now to (give us) greatriches, and protect us who are affluent in (oblations), who utter (your) praise; may we, lord of bay steeds, (be)free from blame on your approach.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And now you, IndraтАФknow us for the sake of great wealth, o lord of men with the mace in your arms,
and guard those generous to us and protect our blameless patrons in your charge, o possessor of fallow bays.

Griffith

And take thou notice of us also, Indra, for ample riches, King whose arm wields thunder!
Protect our wealthy nobles, guard our princes unmenaced near thee, Lord of Tawny Coursers.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSince, royal (Mitra and Varuс╣Зa), the impetuous (Yama) now approaches in expectation of (the gift of)cattle, and desiring praise for the sacrificing (band of the Aс╣Еgirasas); the sage (N─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha) has beenheld most dear by them; may he accomplish (what has to be effected), and make them successful.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

May heaccomplish: liс╣н, may he take away

Jamison Brereton

And now, o you two kings [=Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, or the A┼Ыvins], when in the quest for cattle the hastening one, awakening, makes haste for the bard,
the dearest inspired poet [=Agni?], because he has become theirs
[=patronsтАЩ], will carry them away and will bring them across.

Griffith

When he goes forth, ye Pair of Kings, for booty, speeding to war and praise to please the singer,-
I was the dearest sage of those about him,-let him lead these away and bring them safely.

English translation:

тАЬAnd for the contentment of this victorious (Varuс╣Зa), praising (him) without an effort, we solicit this (ofhim), (that) his progeny, a swift horse, (may be ours), and you, (Varuс╣Зa), are wise, and (are occupied) inprocuring us food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

We solicit this: tat, rebhantaс╕е = praising that (his gift of cows etc.)

Jamison Brereton

And now at the thriving of him [=Agni] who is well bornтАФwe, rasping at will, now beg this: [see vs. 27]тАФ
you, his son, are a hastening horse and an inspired poetтАФas also at the winning of fame.

Griffith

Now for this noble man’s support and comfort, singing with easy voice we thus implore thee:
Impetuous be his son and fleet his courser: and may I be his priest to win him glory.

Geldner

Nun bei dem Gedeihen seines Hausstandes bitten wir, nach Lust lobsingend, darum: Zu eiliger Fahrt sei sein Sohn bereit, sein Ro├Я, und du bist redekundig und dabei, wo man Ruhm gewinnt.

Grassmann

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬIf the priest offers homage to you two (Mitra and Varuс╣Зa) for the sake of your friendship and ourinvigoration, on (the formation of) which (friendship) the praises (of the Aс╣Еgirasas go) everywhere in a commondirection; may he give (plural asure) to the utterer of praise like an ancient road.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Or, like the eastern quarter of theworld

Jamison Brereton

If for the sake of companionship with you two [=Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, or the A┼Ыvins], for us who are his troop, he [=Agni/poet], receiving
[/providing] reverence, finds pleasure in his praise hymnтАФ
he in whom songs in all places come together, like a route with many partsтАФand he does ritual service for the sake of liberality,

Griffith

If, for our strength, the priest with adoration to win your friendship made the laud accepted,
That laud shall be a branching road to virtue for every one to whom the songs are suited.

Geldner

Wenn ich, um euer beider Freundschaft f├╝r uns zu gewinnen, zu einem Loblied auf die Heerschar Lust bekommen habe unter Verbeugungen, so m├╢ge der, zu dem ├╝berall die Lobreden vereint gehen wie ein viel begangener Weg, seiner Gro├Яmut willfahren.

Grassmann

Wenn nun zu eurer beider [des Mitra-Varuna] starken Freundschaft mit uns der Anbeter den Lobgesang zum Genusse darbot, in welchen ├╝berall die Lieder sich vereinen, dann sei er [der Lobgesang] wie ein reich gesegneter Gang f├╢rdernd zu herrlicher Gabe.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAdorable divinities, be consentient for our great preservation, both you who, going in variousdirections, are the bringers of food, and you who, being no longer perplexed, are the discoverers (of the cattle).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Adorable divinities: Aс╣Еgirasas; being no longer perplexed: i.e., by the sixth day’s ceremonials whichN─Бbh─Бnediс╣гс╣нha had enabled them to complete

Jamison Brereton

(…we now beg this:) тАЬO gods worthy of the sacrifice, become joined together for great help for us,
you who, (now) departing, led prizes (here), and who are observers who are never fooled.тАЭ

Griffith

Be to us, then, ye Gods who merit worship, be ye of one accord our strong protection,
Who went on various ways and brought us vigour, ye who are undeceivable explorers.
